| **EHCI V0 ŌĆö probe + port enum** | `drivers/usb/ehci.ad` (NEW) ŌĆö native-Adder USB 2.0 host-controller driver: PCI probe by class triple `0x0C/0x03/0x20`, capability-register decode, BIOSŌåÆOS handoff via the USBLEGSUP extended cap, controller stop + HCRESET, periodic frame list + placeholder async QH, and root-hub port enumeration (power / reset / port-enabled read-back; high-speed devices kept on EHCI, full/low-speed released to a companion). `ehci_init()` wired into `start_kernel` after `xhci_init`; failure non-fatal. Motivation: 2008ŌĆō2014 laptops (the Asus included) often route the built-in keyboard through EHCI rather than the i8042. Verified against QEMU `usb-ehci`. (`d3c978a`) | **Done** |
| **EHCI V1 ŌĆö control transfers + HID keyboard** | Transfer engine: a qTD pool from one `alloc_pages(0)` page (32-byte-aligned), an async-schedule control-transfer QH, and the standard enumeration (GET_DESCRIPTOR / SET_ADDRESS / config-descriptor walk / SET_CONFIGURATION). A HID boot keyboard (class 3 / proto 1) gets SET_PROTOCOL(boot) + SET_IDLE(0) and a periodic interrupt-IN QH; `ehci_poll()` (wired into the timer tick beside `xhci_poll`) drains each 8-byte boot report into the shared kbd FIFO via `hid_kbd_report()`. Verified against QEMU `usb-ehci` + `usb-kbd`: a live `sendkey` keystroke reaches hamsh. (`066f6d3`) | **Done** |
| **EHCI V2 ŌĆö interrupt-driven delivery** | `_ehci_wire_irq()` discovers the PCI MSI capability (cap ID 0x05, e1000e-style cap-walk) and programs single-vector fixed delivery; falls back to PCI INTx via `ioapic_redirect` if no MSI cap. USBINTR enables USBINT + Port Change; `ehci_irq_handler` reads/W1C-acks USBSTS and drains the interrupt-IN QH from interrupt context. Vector 0x43 claimed. The timer-tick `ehci_poll()` is kept as a fallback. **QEMU's `usb-ehci` exposes no PCI cap list and delivers no observable interrupt, so under QEMU the keyboard runs off the poll fallback ŌĆö the IRQ path is code-inspection-verified only, exercised on real ICH/PCH silicon.** (`b3573a2`) | **Partial** |
| **U41 ŌĆö CPython musl static-PIE** | The `u_cpython` build was re-cut as a **musl static-PIE (ET_DYN)** binary. Commit `653d962`'s kernel-image collision guard refuses the old glibc `-static` ET_EXEC (linked at 0x400000, inside the kernel image); glibc `-static-pie` hit a glibc-2.41 `_dl_relocate_static_pie` TLS bug. The musl static-PIE build carries 0 TPOFF64 relocs and loads at a relocated base with no fixed-address overlay. `python3 -c "print(...)"` runs on Hamnix. (`d9f31ca`) | **Done** |
| **U42 ŌĆö busybox musl static-PIE** | The musl busybox fixture was likewise rebuilt as a static-PIE ET_DYN (`-static-pie` via `CFLAGS_busybox` so busybox's `ld -r` partial links don't choke). The 5 busybox applet/pipeline tests (u29/u32/u33/u36/u37) ŌĆö which had SKIP'd since `653d962` refused the old glibc ET_EXEC ŌĆö were re-pointed at it and now **PASS**, exercising real busybox: multi-call banner, applets (`echo`/`cat`/`pwd`/`uname`), `sh -c`, and a 3-stage hamsh pipeline. Two genuine gaps marked **XFAIL**: busybox `ls` directory enumeration prints nothing (musl's `opendir`/`readdir` round-trips the dir fd wrong ŌĆö `getdents64` itself is correct on a direct syscall), and busybox `sh`'s *internal* pipeline (`sh -c "a \| b"`) trips a `#GP`. (`19dd1f4`, `83799d0`) | **Done** |
| **Userland sockets ŌĆö client** | `socket`/`connect`/`read`/`write`/`close` on an `AF_INET` + `SOCK_STREAM` fd bridged to the in-kernel TCP stack ŌĆö for both Linux-ABI binaries and native Adder binaries (native `SYS_SOCKET 41` / `SYS_CONNECT 42` arms in `do_syscall`). `linux_abi/u_socket_state.ad` holds the per-fd backing records; `fs/vfs.ad`'s `FD_SOCKET_MARK` arms route read/write/close. (`e456495`, `f61d70f`) | **Done** |
| **Userland sockets ŌĆö server** | `bind`/`listen`/`accept` bridged to the in-kernel TCP stack's `tcp_listen`/`tcp_accept` ŌĆö `bind` records the port, `listen` calls `tcp_listen`, `accept` returns a fresh socket fd. `user/u_server.ad` + `scripts/test_u_server.sh` prove a userland TCP server. (`3618ee3`) | **Done** |
| **U-resolve ŌĆö userland DNS** | `sys_resolve` ŌĆö a native syscall bridging userland hostname ŌåÆ IPv4 through the in-kernel DNS resolver, so apt can take a `https://deb.debian.org/...` URL by name. (`d44e8d5`) | **Done** |
| **tls_connect(2) ŌĆö userland HTTPS** | `SYS_TLS_CONNECT 277` ŌĆö a kernel-mediated kTLS-shaped bridge: a user binary `connect()`s a socket, then calls `tls_connect(fd, host, hostlen)`; the kernel runs the full TLS 1.3 handshake (X25519 + cert-chain validation + CertificateVerify binding) over the socket's TCP slot and marks the fd TLS-active, so `read`/`write`/`close` thereafter route transparently through the TLS record layer. Per-fd TLS-active flag in `u_socket_state.ad`; a second concurrent handshake returns `-EBUSY` (the tls.ad session state is a single module global). `user/u_tlstest.ad` + `scripts/test_u_tls.sh` verify against a local TLS 1.3 server. (`efad3a9`) | **Done** |
| **apt ŌĆö native package tool** | `user/apt.ad` (NEW) ŌĆö a native Adder `apt`: `apt update <base-url> <suite>` fetches `Release` + `Packages.gz`, gunzips via `lib/zlib/inflate.ad`, stores the index; `apt show <pkg>` / `apt pkgnames` query it as RFC822 stanzas; `apt install <pkg>` resolves transitive `Depends:` (post-order topological install, diamond/cycle-safe, 64-pkg closure), HTTP-downloads each `.deb`, SHA-256-verifies against the index, and hands it to `dpkg -i`. Works over **HTTP and HTTPS** ŌĆö `apt update https://...` reaches a validated TLS connection via `tls_connect(2)`. Verified under QEMU against fake repos. (`f61d70f`, `6459613`, `8984cff`, `b965095`, `3aeaba4`) | **Done** |
| **dpkg V2 ŌĆö dedup + remove** | `dpkg -i` now dedups/replaces an existing status stanza instead of appending duplicates; `dpkg -r <pkg>` removes a package (status stanza + `.list`). (`9bd89e8`) | **Done** |
| **httpd ŌĆö static-file server** | `user/httpd.ad` (NEW) ŌĆö a userland static-file HTTP/1.0 server daemon. (`65534f8`) | **Done** |
| **/var writable tmpfs** | A writable `/var` tmpfs subtree with a boot-time skeleton. **NOTE:** this is a *global* `/var` ŌĆö historical debt against the Namespace law; tracked for migration into the `distrofs` namespace (see TODO Phase C.5). (`86a13bd`) | **Done** |
| **distrofs ŌĆö userland 9P file server** | `user/distrofs.ad` (NEW) ŌĆö a userland 9P file-server daemon exporting a distro-shaped tree (`/var`, `/usr`, `/etc`, ŌĆ”), a Plan 9-pure daemon in the spirit of `rio`/`hamwd`. The intended backing store for all distro / package-manager state, replacing the global `/var`. (`388edb1`) | **Done** |
| **nsrun ŌĆö Plan 9 shim launcher** | `user/nsrun.ad` (NEW) ŌĆö runs a program in a private namespace: `rfork(RFNAMEG)` ŌåÆ mount `distrofs` so the child sees `/var`, `/usr`, `/etc` through 9P, isolated from the parent namespace ŌåÆ exec. Per-pid `/srv` post names. (`1707c7b`, `3d5c283`) | **Done** |
| **distrorun bind fix** | `user/distrorun.ad` now grafts the initramfs subtrees with `bind()` rather than `mount()`, matching the Plan 9 namespace shape. (`5e6a241`) | **Done** |
| **9P V4.1 ŌĆö create over a real fd** | `p9c_create` + create-on-write-open over a real fd in the kernel 9P client (`sys/src/9/port/9p_client.ad` + `chan.ad`). (`498c416`) | **Done** |
| **9P conn-table lifecycle** | `p9_conns` are now released on unmount + on task exit, closing a connection-table leak. (`cc11519`) | **Done** |
| **TCP ephemeral-port rotation** | `drivers/net/tcp.ad` rotates the ephemeral source port per active-open `connect`, fixing back-to-back connects (e.g. apt's Release-then-Packages.gz fetches) that previously wedged the handshake by reusing one port. This let apt drop its install-path source-port workaround. (`d5f14f0`, `3aeaba4`) | **Done** |
| **Per-task kernel stack 4ŌåÆ16 KiB** | `KSTACK_SIZE` 4 KiB ŌåÆ 16 KiB (`KSTACK_ORDER 2`) in `kernel/sched/core.ad`. The TLS 1.3 handshake is the deepest in-kernel call chain (X25519 + AES-256 key schedule + SHA-256 + cert-chain parse + HKDF) and was overrunning the 4 KiB kstack into the task's adjacent user stack ŌĆö corrupting `apt`'s `tls_connect(2)` return address. Part of the apt-HTTPS-crash fix, which also made `_http_get` honour `Content-Length` and switched `tcp_recv`'s deadline from frozen jiffies to an iteration count. (`8c87e72`) | **Done** |
| **build_iso.sh SIGPIPE fix** | `scripts/build_iso.sh` no longer reports a spurious "multiboot1 magic not found" ŌĆö a SIGPIPE race in the magic-check pipeline. (`a73e5fb`) | **Done** |

The headline of this wave: as of M16.156, Hamnix boots all the way
to the `hamsh` shell on a real Asus i5-4210U (Haswell ULT) laptop in
**Legacy/BIOS mode** ŌĆö earlier the project only ran under QEMU/KVM +
OVMF. Open on metal: the laptop's built-in keyboard does not respond
(leading hypothesis: it is EHCI-routed, not on the i8042 ŌĆö an EHCI
driver is in flight), and UEFI boot on the real Asus has not been
re-confirmed since the M16.151ŌĆō156 wave.

### Wave since the apt / EHCI / userland-sockets refresh

These rows land everything between commit `0bb2e1c` (the STATUS /
README / TODO refresh that closed the apt-userland wave) and
`c4deb00`. The headline: the kernel's **memory model became real** ŌĆö
the kernel relocated to the higher half, forked children get a fully
private (and now copy-on-write) address space, and large VMAs are
backed by multiple buddy chunks. Plus a round of Adder compiler
correctness fixes and build/test-harness hygiene.

| Item | Description | Status |
|------|-------------|--------|
| **fork() ŌĆö real per-process address space** | Hamnix had run every ET_DYN user binary identity-mapped (user vaddr == physical) with every task's PML4 a verbatim clone of the BSP's and all lower page tables shared; `fork()` only handed the child a different *physical* stack page at a *different* virtual address, so the child's inherited absolute pointers (saved `%rbp` chain, return addresses, glibc's `_IO_2_1_stdout_`, the TCB at `fs_base`, the malloc arena header) all still pointed at the parent's memory. A child returning through glibc's fork epilogue aborted in sysmalloc. The fork path now eager-copies the whole ELF image (code+data+bss), the entire reserved brk heap `[brk_base, brk_max)`, the whole user stack, and every anonymous/file-backed mmap VMA ŌĆö each into private physical pages remapped at the **same** vaddr in the child's PML4, so inherited pointers stay valid and the two processes never share writable memory. `fs/elf.ad` records the loaded image span and gains `vm_fork_copy_range` / `vm_fork_install_all`; `mm/vma.ad` gains `vma_fork_copy`; `do_rfork` (Plan 9 new-process path) reuses the same machinery, dropping the fragile per-page `%rbp` translation; `TaskStruct` records `image_lo/hi` + `ustack_lo/sz` and the Linux user stack grows to 256 KiB. Shipped with the `%rdi` syscall-ABI fix ŌĆö `syscall_64.S` had zeroed `%rdi` on the non-FUTEX exit path (a stale U27 glibc workaround), corrupting musl's `open()`/`opendir()` which keeps the just-opened fd in `%rdi` across an `fcntl` syscall ŌĆö so busybox `ls` enumerated nothing; restoring `%rdi` from its saved slot collapses the dead per-`nr` FUTEX branch and makes `test_u32 busybox ls` XPASS. Also shipped: `scripts/_qemu_drive.sh`, a prompt-aware QEMU harness that waits for hamsh's `[hamsh] M16.35 shell ready` banner before feeding each command (the old fixed `sleep 3` lost input to the bufferless 16550 RX FIFO as boots got slower), and an atkbd-diag gate so the periodic `[atkbd-diag]` line stays silent on QEMU until a real PS/2 byte arrives. Verified: a 20-round concurrent malloc/free fork stress, `test_u26_fork`, `test_rfork`, `test_u37`, the musl/glibc thread suites all PASS. (`e021700`, `633dad2`, `33510d7`) | **Done** |
| **VMA allocator ŌĆö multi-chunk backing** | `vma_alloc` capped a single VMA-backed allocation at 4 MiB ŌĆö the buddy allocator's `MAX_ORDER` chunk ŌĆö so a glibc pthread's default 8 MiB thread stack failed with `vma: alloc len=8392704 exceeds MAX_ORDER` and `test_u28_glibc_thread` FAILed. A VMA whose page-rounded length exceeds 4 MiB is now backed by several buddy chunks (each Ōēż 4 MiB) carved from a dedicated exclusive virtual window `[1 GiB, 4 GiB)` and overlaid into the task's PML4 via `elf_install_user_mapping` so `[base, base+length)` presents one contiguous virtual range; `VmaNode` grows a `(chunks, nchunks)` pair pointing at a kmalloc'd `VmaChunk` array. `vma_fork_copy` detects multi-chunk VMAs and copies every chunk into the child. Exposing the 8 MiB stack also uncovered two latent thread-start bugs: a `CLONE_VM` thread now shares the creator's PML4 (correct semantics ŌĆö the creator's multi-chunk overlays were otherwise invisible and the thread `#UD`'d on its own stack); and `do_clone` / `create_user_thread` now carry `%rdx`/`%r8` into the child for glibc's `clone3.S` convention (Hamnix had only propagated `%r9`, musl's). `test_u28_glibc_thread` now PASSes. (`b8e0398`) | **Done** |
| **Higher-half kernel relocation** | The kernel previously ran identity-mapped in the LOW virtual address space, colliding with non-PIE `ET_EXEC` Linux binaries (linked at `0x400000`, with brk/mmap extending straight into the identity-mapped kernel image ŌĆö `fs/elf.ad` explicitly refused such binaries with "needs a higher-half kernel"). The kernel is now relocated to the canonical x86_64 base `0xffffffff80000000` (PML4 entry 511), vacating the entire lower canonical half for userland. Boot format switched **`elf32-i386` ŌåÆ `elf64-x86-64`** (elf32 cannot represent symbol addresses above 4 GiB); `vmlinux.lds` splits LMA from VMA ŌĆö a LOW boot region (multiboot header, 32-bit `_start`, `gdt64`) at VMA==LMA `0x100000`, and the HIGH-half region linked at `0xffffffff80000000+offset` with `AT()` pinning each segment's `p_paddr` low. `header.S`'s 32-bit `_start` builds page tables mapping the image at both the low identity address and the higher half, then `movabsq`-jumps RIP into the high half; the UEFI stub gets the same mapping plus a 64-bit-ELF program-header parser. New `virt_to_phys`/`phys_to_virt` (`arch/x86/mm/pgtable.ad`) rebase high-half kernel addresses for device DMA (virtio / e1000e / r8169 ring writes, AHCI PRDT, NVMe PRP). The ELF loader's kernel-image collision guard is removed ŌĆö a fixed-address `ET_EXEC` at `0x400000` now loads and runs (`test_u7_mmap`: `elf64: ET_EXEC user-map: [0x400000, 0x403000)`). Hand-written asm `.long sym; .long 0` IDT/IRQ stub splits become `.quad sym`. Since QEMU's `-kernel` multiboot1 loader rejects 64-bit ELFs, tests boot via `scripts/_kernel_iso.sh` ŌĆö a `build/binshim/qemu-system-x86_64` PATH shim that transparently boots an `ELFCLASS64` `-kernel` target from a BIOS GRUB ISO. The follow-up ESP fix enlarges the FAT12 ESP `8 MiB ŌåÆ 24 MiB` (the elf64 higher-half kernel grew to ~10 MB and overflowed the old volume). (`406c313`, `da065ec`) | **Done** |
| **Core-stabilization** | Three independent stabilization fixes. (a) The Adder compiler now supports **string-literal-initialised globals**: `gen_data`'s `emit_init` only accepted an `IntLiteral` initialiser, so an `Array[N, uint8]` global could not be initialised from a string literal ŌĆö every kernel string constant had to be materialised byte-by-byte at runtime via scattered `_init_*()` fill workarounds; `emit_init` now emits a `StringLiteral` initialiser's bytes straight into `.data`, NUL-padded to the declared length. (b) The **U9 nested-frame-`Array` bug** ŌĆö calling `_u_open()` from `_u_openat()` deterministically returned `-ENOENT` ŌĆö is confirmed **already-fixed and dead**: it was a downstream symptom of two codegen defects fixed independently (`224051b` `&arr[i][j]` address-of miscompile, `18534b2` sub-8-byte scalar `movq` store/load); the hand-inlined `_u_openat` workaround is removed and the binary delegates to `_u_open()` again, verified by `test_u9_access`. (c) Fixed-`sleep` test harnesses (`test_u7_mmap`, `test_coreutils`, `test_u18_glibc_hello`, `test_u27_musl_thread`, `test_u28_glibc_thread`) migrated to the prompt-aware `_qemu_drive` harness that waits for hamsh's banner before sending input. (`e8be7f6`, `61176e3`, `edee7b5`) | **Done** |
| **Signed/unsigned shift + divide codegen** | The x86_64 backend lowered `>>`, `/`, `//` and `%` to the **unsigned** machine instructions unconditionally (`shrq` for every right shift, `divq` for every divide/modulo) under a stale "Adder ints are non-negative" comment ŌĆö x86 carries signedness in the instruction, so this miscompiled signed arithmetic. New `_binop_signed_op(left, right)` helper (mirroring the comparison-signedness machinery at `a5a7e55`, reusing `_is_unsigned_type`): `>>` now picks `sarq` (arithmetic, sign-extend) vs `shrq` (logical), and `/`/`%` pick `cqo; idivq` vs `xorq %rdx,%rdx; divq`, by operand type. Following C's usual-arithmetic-conversion rule, unsigned wins on a mixed-sign pair and an all-unknown pair stays unsigned (preserving the long-standing default ŌĆö Adder kernel code is overwhelmingly unsigned `uint64` bit math); `<<` is unchanged (`shlq` is correct for both). New `tests/test_compiler_unsigned_divshift.ad` fixture wired into the compiler suite. (`255e1ff`) | **Done** |
| **Per-module symbol scoping** | Adder's `merge_programs()` flattened every module's top-level declarations into one `Program` keyed by a single global `seen_names` dict, so two `.ad` files each defining a private helper of the same natural name (`_emit_str`, `_helper`, ŌĆ”) was a hard error ŌĆö developers and agents had to rename helpers per file (`_ci_emit_str`/`_mi_emit_str`, `_up_`/`_la_` prefixes). Adder now has real per-module scoping by **convention** (no new keyword): a leading-underscore top-level name is module-private, mangled to `<module_slug>__<name>` with every intra-module reference rewritten to match before codegen; non-underscore names stay globally visible. The `import` statement IS the export annotation ŌĆö a private name another module does `from M import _name` for is promoted back to public and left un-mangled (audit found exactly four: `_add_export`, `__stack_chk_fail/guard/init`, `_u_errstr`). `ExternDecl` names are never mangled; a genuine collision of two public names is still a hard error. No migration of the ~350 existing `.ad` files needed. `ast_nodes.py` grows `module`/`orig_name` fields; `adder.py` runs `resolve_module_scopes()` in `merge_programs()`; the codegen stack-protector skip-list matches against `orig_name`. (`7415db3`) | **Done** |
| **CI fix** | Every CI run failed at "Compile bare-metal kernel" ŌĆö `ld` reported undefined references to `initramfs_cpio_base` / `initramfs_cpio_size`, symbols that live in the generated, gitignored `fs/initramfs_blob.S` (absent from a fresh CI checkout, never regenerated). The GitHub workflow now builds userland first, runs `build_initramfs.py` to emit `fs/initramfs_blob.S`, then compiles the kernel ŌĆö CI is green again. (`179f9a5`) | **Done** |
| **Build hygiene** | Two test-harness reliability fixes. (a) A hard-killed build leaves truncated `.elf`/blob artifacts the incremental rebuild won't regenerate, silently poisoning the next test; `_build_lock.sh` now auto-wipes the compiled-output surface (`build/user`, `build/mod`, `build/iso`, `build/*.elf`, `build/*.iso`, `fs/initramfs_blob.S`) once per test under the lock it already holds ŌĆö disk images `build/*.img` are spared. (b) **Build-on-missing fixtures**: the gitignored `tests/u-binary/u_<name>` fixtures are absent from every fresh `git worktree`, and each `test_u*.sh`'s hand-rolled "skip-on-missing" block printed a SKIP + `exit 0` ŌĆö dispatched agents silently under-verified the U-track and misreported a missing toolchain. New `scripts/_ensure_ubin.sh` (`ensure_ubin` / `ensure_ubin_or_skip`) builds the fixture from source on demand and only SKIPs on a genuine build failure; all 38 affected scripts wired to it, and `test_u34`/`u35` migrated off the retired glibc-static `u_busybox` onto the musl static-PIE `u_busybox_musl`. (`eb2eedd`, `b505db1`) | **Done** |
| **fork() ŌĆö copy-on-write** | `fork()` had given each child a private address space by eager-copying every writable region (~33 MiB: ELF image, the 32 MiB brk reservation, the user stack, TLS/TCB) into fresh pages. That is now replaced with copy-on-write. `mm/cow.ad` adds a per-physical-page refcount table (one `uint16` per PFN) carved from memblock in `mem_init()` before the buddy allocator starts. On fork (`do_clone` / `do_rfork`), `vm_cow_share_all()` walks every writable user page and, in both parent and child PML4s, marks it read-only and sets a COW marker in **PTE bit 9** (software-available), pointing both PML4s at the same physical page and bumping its refcount. The `#PF` handler (vector 14) is now productive: a write fault to a present, read-only, COW-marked page is resolved by `do_page_fault` ŌĆö refcount 1 just clears the marker in place, otherwise a fresh page is allocated, bytes copied, the faulting PTE repointed, the old page's refcount dropped, the TLB invalidated; a non-COW write fault keeps the diagnostic-halt behaviour so real segfaults are not masked. Two root-cause fixes were needed: `cow_init()` snapshots the pristine boot CR3 (and `create_user_thread()` clones the pristine boot PML4, not the live CR3) so the table-cracker can tell a still-shared boot mapping from a private one; and the ELF32 loader records the loaded image span so native binaries' `.data`/`.bss` are COW-shared on fork. `CLONE_VM` threads are unaffected (they share the creator's PML4 outright and never enter the COW machinery). Deferred at this commit: mmap VMAs keep the eager-copy path ŌĆö closed the next wave by `ea58371` (see below). Verified by `scripts/test_cow_fork.sh` (new 8-iteration fork stress) plus the fork/thread/coreutils/boot/compiler suites. (`d6a34a7`) | **Done** |

### Wave since the copy-on-write fork refresh

These rows land everything between commit `c4deb00` (the memory
note that closed the higher-half / COW-fork wave) and `1205ab3`.
The headline: the kernel's **scheduler became preemptive** ŌĆö a
tight-looping userland task can no longer hang the box ŌĆö fork's
copy-on-write was extended over the whole address space, a native
**SSH-2.0 server** went interactive, and `apt` can now fetch,
decompress, and **cryptographically verify** a real Debian `main`-
sized signed index over HTTPS.

| Item | Description | Status |
|------|-------------|--------|
| **mmap-VMA copy-on-write** | `d6a34a7` made the ELF image, brk heap, and user stack COW-shared on fork but deliberately left mmap VMAs on the eager-copy (`alloc` + `memcpy`) path. This finishes the job ŌĆö **the whole forked address space is now copy-on-write**. `vma_fork_copy` (`mm/vma.ad`) COW-shares each owner VMA's pages via `vm_cow_share_range`: every page across `[start, end)` is marked read-only + COW bit-9 in BOTH parent and child PML4s pointing at the same physical page, and the per-PFN refcount is bumped. Single-chunk and multi-chunk VMAs take the same path; alias VMAs (`MAP_FIXED` slices) stay a metadata-only copy so their pages are not COW-shared twice via the enclosing owner node. Because a VMA page can now be shared, `_vma_node_free` must free through the refcount: a COW node (new `is_cow` flag, reusing the old `pad0` slot) is freed by walking the owning task's page table over `[start, end)` and routing each physical page through `cow_drop_page` ŌĆö the page returns to the buddy allocator only when its refcount hits 0. The page table, not the recorded backing run, is ground truth, because COW resolution can repoint individual PTEs at fresh pages; this covers every VMA-page free path ŌĆö `munmap` (`_vma_carve_range`) and execve / task-teardown (`vma_clear`). Non-COW VMAs keep the fast bulk `free_pages` path; `CLONE_VM` threads never enter the COW path. New `tests/u-binary/src/mmap_fork` (a Linux-ABI asm fixture that mmaps + COW-forks + verifies parent/child privacy + munmaps over 8 iterations) and `scripts/test_mmap_fork.sh`. (`ea58371`) | **Done** |
| **dead-workaround cleanup** | A round of cleanups removing now-obsolete Adder-compiler-bug workarounds, each made dead by a real compiler fix that has since landed on `main`. (a) `name: Array[N, uint8] = "literal"` string-literal-initialised globals work (`codegen_x86.py` `emit_init`), so the scattered `_init_*()` runtime byte-by-byte fill workarounds are replaced with direct string-literal initializers across `user/nsrun.ad`, `user/p9srv_demo.ad`, `user/distrofs.ad`, `user/base64.ad`, `tests/test_nsrun.ad`, `tests/test_distrofs.ad`, and `drivers/net/tls.ad`'s 98-byte CertificateVerify prefix ŌĆö emitted bytes byte-identical (objdump-verified). (b) The U9 nested-frame-`Array` miscompile is dead (downstream of `224051b` + `18534b2`), so two scratch arrays hoisted to top-level BSS to dodge it ŌĆö `lib/zlib/inflate.ad`'s `hf_offsets` and `user/hamsh.ad`'s `expand_name_tmp` ŌĆö move back to function-locals (a top-level "local" is shared across calls / re-entrancy, a latent hazard). (c) Since U14.5 (`a5a7e55`) `<` on `uint64` operands emits the unsigned `setb`, so `drivers/net/tls.ad`'s 128-bit-carry XOR-flip add-overflow workaround is dropped for the natural `new_lo < cur_lo` test, and `fs/elf.ad`'s `have_lowest`-flag minimum search reverts to the natural `UINT{64,32}_MAX` sentinel in both PT_LOAD span passes. Behaviour preserved throughout. (`279e279`, `b7e45e3`, `e3a45e9`, `e63e2e1`) | **Done** |
| **build / docs hygiene** | Two small fixes. (a) The PynuxŌåÆAdder rename (`3189ce8`) renamed source files `.py`ŌåÆ`.ad` but left stale `.py` references in 42 files' header comments and cross-references (e.g. `kernel/block/blk.ad` still opened `# kernel/block/blk.py`) ŌĆö all rewritten to `.ad`; genuine Python references (the CPython-hosted `compiler/*.py`, the `scripts/*.py` build scripts) left intact. (b) `ceb3194` used `git add -A` and accidentally committed two compiled binaries (`tests/u-binary/busybox`, `tests/u-binary/src/mmap_fork/mmap_fork`) ŌĆö untracked them and added the missing `.gitignore` entries. (`ceb3194`, `4c6e2b0`) | **Done** |
| **apt over a live Debian mirror** | An investigate-and-fix pass making userland `apt` work against the real `deb.debian.org` mirror over the internet (QEMU SLIRP NAT). Real bugs fixed across the stack: a free-running PIT channel-0 microsecond clock (`pit_monotonic_us()`, `arch/x86/kernel/time.ad`) because `jiffies` freezes whenever `EFLAGS.IF` is masked and a SYSCALL clears IF ŌĆö so a `while get_jiffies() < deadline` loop inside a `read()`/`write()` syscall spun forever; `_tls_read_record` reads exactly the current TLS record's bytes instead of over-reading into an 8 KiB spill buffer that overflowed on real multi-record Debian `Release` files; a real TCP receive-window advertisement (`_tcp_adv_window`) advertising actual free ring space for large transfers; the tmpfs per-file cap raised 4 KiB ŌåÆ 512 KiB (lazily kmalloc'd); and `apt update` taking an optional component argument. New `scripts/test_apt_live.sh` (a network test, deliberately not in CI). (`a28bf82`) | **Done** |
| **xz / LZMA2 decompression** | `lib/xz/xz.ad` (NEW) ŌĆö an xz/LZMA2 decompressor. An inherited WIP decoder declared a `dict_start` field but fed the global `total_pos` to every position-state / literal-context / back-reference-reach decision; single-block streams worked by accident, but the moment a second xz block (or any dict-reset chunk) began, the range coder desynced. Fixed with a `_dict_pos()` helper (`total_pos - dict_start`) routing the literal decoder, the pos-state, and the reach check through the dictionary-relative position, and by advancing `dict_start` on every dictionary reset; the 96 KiB multi-block fixture round-trips byte-exact. Wired into `user/apt.ad`: `apt update` probes the modern `Packages.xz` (LZMA2) index FIRST and routes the body through `xz_decompress()`, falling back to the gzip `Packages.gz` inflater only when `.xz` is absent. New `scripts/test_xz.sh` + `scripts/test_apt_xz.sh` (an xz-only repo index). (`78a5dfa`, `37c966b`) | **Done** |
| **apt ŌĆö full-size streaming index** | `apt` buffered the whole compressed download and the whole decompressed index in fixed 256 KiB BSS arenas, so it only ever worked against fixture-sized repos. A real Debian `main/binary-amd64/Packages` is multi-MB compressed / tens of MB decompressed ŌĆö far past those caps. `apt update` now **streams the gz index end to end**: the compressed body is drained off the socket 64 KiB at a time, fed to the resumable gzip inflater 64 KiB at a time, and the decompressed bytes flow through an incremental RFC822-stanza counter and an incremental writer to `/tmp/apt/Packages` ŌĆö nothing holds the whole index. To make this possible the gzip inflater (`lib/zlib/inflate.ad`) now treats a full `out_buf` as a YIELD (`out_full=1`), not an error, with every emit site resumable; callers that size `out_buf` to the whole output never see the yield. New `scripts/test_apt_large.sh` fabricates a Debian-`main`-shaped fixture (12000 stanzas, ~3.9 MB decompressed / ~330 KB gz). (`3d64c48`) | **Done** |
| **apt ŌĆö InRelease GPG verification** | Userland `apt` fetched a repository's index but trusted it on transport security alone ŌĆö a MITM or malicious mirror could serve a forged index. `apt update` now fetches the inline-clearsigned `InRelease`, verifies its OpenPGP signature against a baked archive key, and refuses the repository outright on a bad signature. New `lib/pgp/pgp.ad` parses the OpenPGP packet stream (RFC 4880): the v4 RSA Public-Key and signature packets, radix-64 de-armor, and the cleartext-signature framework, assembling the exact v4 signed-data byte string; verification reuses `lib/rsa`'s `rsa_pkcs1_v1_5_verify`. The trust anchor is baked into the initramfs at `/etc/apt-trusted.gpg` (the host's `debian-archive-keyring.gpg` by default). `apt update` enforces it ŌĆö verified ŌåÆ proceed; signature invalid ŌåÆ HARD ABORT before touching the index; `InRelease` absent / no keyring ŌåÆ a loud UNAUTHENTICATED warning then proceed. A follow-up closed two gaps that blocked verification against the **genuine `deb.debian.org` archive**, which signs `Release`/`InRelease` with SHA-512 and ships a multi-key keyring: new `lib/sha2/sha2.ad` (userland SHA-512/384, a re-namespaced port of the kernel TLS engine), `rsa_pkcs1_v1_5_verify` gained a `digest_alg` selector (SHA-256/384/512 EMSA-PKCS1-v1_5 DigestInfo prefixes), and `PgpKeyring` now holds every RSA Public-Key packet in a keyring blob ŌĆö `apt` verifies the signature against each key in turn and succeeds if any trusted key accepts it. New `scripts/test_apt_inrelease.sh` + `scripts/test_apt_inrelease_sha512.sh`. (`b4c59fa`, `2064d29`) | **Done** |
| **SSH-2.0 server** | `user/sshd.ad` (NEW) ŌĆö a from-scratch SSH-2.0 server in Adder that lets a real OpenSSH client connect into a Hamnix guest on port 22. SSH layers (all verified against OpenSSH 10): the transport binary-packet protocol + `SSH_MSG_KEXINIT` negotiation (RFC 4253); `curve25519-sha256` key exchange (X25519 ECDH + SHA-256, exchange hash, `SSH_MSG_NEWKEYS`); an `ecdsa-sha2-nistp256` host key signed via new ECDSA-P256 signing; `chacha20-poly1305@openssh.com` for the encrypted stream; `password` user auth (RFC 4252, root / hamnix); and one `session` channel with pty-req + shell, hamsh spawned and bridged to the channel via two pipes (RFC 4254). New self-contained crypto for the CPL-3 binary: `lib/ssh/sshcrypto.ad` (ChaCha20, Poly1305, X25519, ported from the kernel `drivers/net/tls.ad` primitives) and `lib/ssh/sshsign.ad` (ECDSA-P256 signing, reusing `lib/ec/p256.ad`). Kernel support: `SYS_READ_NB` (23) + `vfs_read_nb` + `tcp_recv_nb` / `tcp_slot_at_eof` for a single-task socket+pipe poll loop, and a `SYS_SPAWN` `-1` ("inherit") stdin/stdout fd now dups the parent's fd 0/1. `scripts/test_sshd.sh`. (`03a3a18`) | **Done** |
| **SSH session ŌĆö interactive** | The native sshd authenticated and opened a session channel, but nothing hamsh (or any command it ran) produced ever came back to the client. Root cause: Hamnix multitasked **cooperatively** ŌĆö a task lost the CPU only inside a blocking syscall ŌĆö and sshd's SSHŌåöhamsh bridge is by design a single-task non-blocking poll loop, so its idle throttle `_short_sleep()` (a pure userland spin on `sys_get_jiffies()`) never yielded; the spawned hamsh and every command it would spawn were starved forever. Fix: a new `SYS_YIELD` (24) syscall calling `yield_to_others()` (the same cooperative-rotation primitive `SYS_WAITPID` and the blocking pipe path use), with `sshd`'s `_short_sleep()` rewired to call it. `test_sshd.sh` now REQUIRES tier 3 ŌĆö ssh in, run `uname`, assert its output (`Hamnix x86_64 0.1`) round-trips over the channel. (`f800cce`) | **Done** |
| **preemptive scheduling** | Hamnix multitasked **purely cooperatively** ŌĆö a task yielded the CPU only inside a blocking syscall (`waitpid`, a blocking pipe/stdin read, `yield`) ŌĆö so a tight-looping userland task that made no blocking syscall starved every other task forever; one bad process hung the box. `timer_interrupt()` already called `schedule()` on every 100 Hz tick, but it switched out of *any* context (including ring-0 kthread / IRQ code, where preempting half-updated kernel state is unsafe), and the real workload never had two concurrent `STATE_READY` user tasks, so the switch always early-returned. This makes preemption real and safe: `irq_asm.S` passes the interrupted CS through `do_irq()` to `timer_interrupt()`; **preemption-point policy V1** preempts ONLY when the timer caught ring 3 (userland) ŌĆö ring-0 ticks never switch (the cooperative yields already cover kernel context), and SYSCALL masks IF so the timer cannot fire mid-syscall anyway; a per-task quantum (`SCHED_QUANTUM_TICKS = 5` ticks) is aged each tick by `preempt_tick()` and signals a switch only when spent, the tick hit ring 3, and another task is `STATE_READY`; `schedule()` re-arms the quantum on every switch (preemptive or cooperative). The IRQ-frame context switch reuses the existing `schedule()` / `__switch_to_asm` path ŌĆö the interrupted task's full state already lives on its kstack, and when rescheduled it unwinds back through `do_irq` / `common_irq`'s `iretq` into the exact userland instruction it was preempted at. `timer_interrupt()` now EOIs the LAPIC itself before any possible context switch (a deferred EOI would leave the in-service bit set across the switch and starve the incoming task of timer IRQs). (`1205ab3`) | **Done** |

The headline of this wave: Hamnix's scheduler is no longer
cooperative-only ŌĆö the 100 Hz timer can now preempt a CPU-bound
ring-3 task, so a runaway userland process can no longer hang the
machine (kernel context stays cooperative, which is safe). With
mmap-VMA COW the entire forked address space is copy-on-write, and
`apt` can fetch, xz/gz-decompress, stream, and OpenPGP-verify a real
Debian `main`-sized signed index over HTTPS ŌĆö all verified under
QEMU.

Surface area below targets the actual end-game.

Goal: run unmodified Linux server binaries on top of Hamnix
ŌĆö a useful **server OS** that can be installed on real
hardware, boot from disk, and host services. Targets:
Python 3, Apache/nginx, OpenSSH, PostgreSQL, the Debian
package manager itself. **Graphics is console-only (VGA text
+ EFI GOP text-mode framebuffer); X11 / Wayland / Steam /
Firefox / any GUI app are explicitly out of scope.** Implies:

- Linux x86_64 syscall ABI under the stock numbers (read=0,
  write=1, ŌĆ”, openat=257, futex=202, etc.). Hamnix's own
  syscalls move to a high-number range (1000+) to avoid
  collision.
- `/lib/ld-linux-x86-64.so.2` dynamic linker ŌĆö either Hamnix-
  authored or wrapping Debian's. Required for apt-installed
  dynamic binaries (everything in Debian).
- Glibc / musl compatibility ŌĆö the layers between syscalls
  and what apps actually call.
- `/proc` and `/sys` layouts that satisfy glibc's runtime
  setup + udev-style device introspection.
- Threading primitives ŌĆö `futex(2)`, `clone(CLONE_THREAD)`,
  TLS via `arch_prctl(ARCH_SET_FS)`.
- Mmap layout that matches what loaders assume.
- TCP/IP networking ŌĆö apt fetches over HTTP(S); a server OS
  must accept inbound connections (ssh, web).

## Wave ŌĆö 2026-05-22 / 2026-05-23: real-hardware boot + Plan-9 networking + live-Debian apt + install-over-SSH demo

Real-hardware bring-up arc on an Intel NUC and an Asus i5-4210U
(Haswell ULT) laptop. The NUC reaches a working `hamsh` prompt on the
**default ISO with no env-var overrides** ŌĆö end-game goal #1 (UEFI/
Legacy boot on real hardware) is now closed for that box; the Asus is
one re-flash away from the same.

| Item | Description | Status |
|------|-------------|--------|
| **/net 9P file tree** | TCP, UDP, and ICMP exposed as `/net/<proto>/clone` + `/net/<proto>/N/{ctl,data,status,local,remote}` (`drivers/net/devnet.ad`). Native code dials via `user/net9.ad`. Linux `socket()/connect()/bind()/listen()/accept()` retired from Layer 1 ŌĆö they live only in `linux_abi/u_syscalls.ad` as Layer-2 consumers of `/net`. **Layer 1 exposes zero BSD socket syscalls.** Migrated: in-kernel `http_get`, apt-HTTP, apt-HTTPS, `u_tlstest`, `u_server`, sshd, httpd. (`8e70852`, `9402fc7`, `145837d`, `4f05307`, `747844d`) | Done |
| **TLS over `/net`** | TLS 1.3 record-layer transport is a `/net` connection (`_tls_wire_send`/`_tls_wire_recv`). A `tls <hostname>` ctl on a connected `/net/tcp` conn upgrades it to TLS. (`9402fc7`..`747844d`) | Done |
| **Native `ping` via `/net/icmp`** | Plan-9-shape ICMP as the third `/net` proto. `user/ping.ad` is a native-Adder ping with `-c`/`-i`/hostname resolution via `sys_resolve`. Plus hamsh lexer fix to lex IPv4 literals as a single `TK_WORD`. (`0782728`, `7dc8450`, `d97c3aa`) | Done |
| **IP loopback shortcut** | `drivers/net/ip.ad::ip_send` detects 127.0.0.0/8 destinations BEFORE the MAC/ARP/eth_tx path and injects the IPv4 packet straight back into `ip_rx`. `ping 127.0.0.1` works without a NIC. (`62fbac3`) | Done |
| **Clean linux/debian namespace** | `linuxruntime` ŌåÆ `linux` in `/etc/rc.boot`, with a duplicate-body `debian` alias. New `ns clean { ŌĆ” }` modifier flips rfork to `RFCNAMEG` (hermetic) at enter-time. Kernel-side `bind / OLD` support in `sys/src/9/port/chan.ad`'s prefix matcher. The `linux` ns binds: `/` ŌåÆ distro tree, `/home` (host shared), `/dev`, `/proc`, `/srv`, `/n`. Real isolation test plants an ambient `bind /sentinel_host ŌĆ”` and asserts it does NOT leak. (`07c3063`, `6cb0dfd`) | Done |
| **Busybox in default distro tree** | `tests/u-binary/u_busybox_musl` auto-staged into `/var/lib/distros/default/bin/busybox`, applet S_IFLNK symlinks for sh/ash/ls/cat/echo/cp/mv/rm/mkdir/pwd/grep/head/tail/wc/true/false/env/printf/date/sleep/basename/dirname (22 applets). `fs/cpio.ad` extended with `mode` field on `FileEntry`; `fs/vfs.ad::_lookup_name` follows S_IFLNK chains. ~1.0 MiB initramfs delta. `enter linux { /bin/sh }` works out of the box on a vanilla ISO. (`1115f5d`) | Done |
| **EFI memory-map walker** | UEFI path consumes the firmware's `EFI_MEMORY_DESCRIPTOR` array via `GetMemoryMap`. `arch/x86/mm/e820.ad` walker ŌåÆ memblock-free ranges, unlocking RAM > 240 MiB on UEFI (`[memblock] free: 935 MiB` at `-m 1G`). `7365746` made it robust against real laptop firmware (100ŌĆō300 descriptors at 96/128-byte stride): buffer 16 KiB ŌåÆ 64 KiB, explicit return-value check on GetMemoryMap, falls back cleanly to conservative window on failure. (`83f8de8`, `2fb1eb6`, `7365746`) | Done |
| **Bare-metal xHCI auto-skip** | `_xhci_v1_bringup`'s HCH-clear MMIO poll stalls the CPU on real NUC silicon (load instruction itself doesn't retire ŌĆö no software-side timeout helps). `xhci_init` checks CPUID 0x40000000 (`is_bare_metal() ŌåÆ ebx == 0`); on bare metal it auto-skips, with `ENABLE_XHCI_FORCE_INIT=1` and `ENABLE_XHCI_NO_INIT=1` overrides. Decision matrix: explicit markers always win, otherwise CPUID predicate decides. Plus dense `[boot:01.f.a..n]` inner sub-checkpoints inside `_xhci_v1_attach_keyboard` (`6381302`) and an `/etc/xhci-no-attach` escape hatch. EHCI/AHCI/NVMe vulnerable to the same class of stall ŌĆö audited, fixes flagged for future. (`71961b3`, `6381302`, `8b1ab21`, `4ba3bc9`) | Done |
| **Per-task ELF mapping** | The marquee kernel fix. Three ELF load paths (`fs/elf.ad::_load_elf64` ET_DYN, `elf_load_blob` ELF32, the user-stack alloc, `_u_brk`'s lazy reservation) silently relied on the BSP's 1 GiB PS=1 identity-map stamp. On QEMU this worked by accident (allocator returned low phys, identity map covered hamsh). On Asus the allocator returned phys outside the identity range, so SYSRETQ landed in ring-3 and the first instruction-fetch read garbage from phys 0x100c04012. Fixed with `elf_install_user_range` cracking the PS=1 page and installing per-task PDPT ŌåÆ PD ŌåÆ PT chains ending in 4 KiB PTEs with `P\|RW\|US\|NX-or-X`, applied to every PT_LOAD + user stack + brk heap. Latent secondary fix: `elf_install_user_mapping` switched from `get_bsp_cr3()` (live `%cr3`) to `cow_boot_cr3()` (snapshot) ŌĆö `test_cow_fork` exposed PDPT-corruption that would have hit fork-spawn paths. (`61e2b24`) | Done |
| **Console split + framebuffer ANSI** | `early_putc()` was a single fan-out for kernel `printk` AND every userland write, unconditionally prepending `[NNNNNN] ` timestamps. New `early_putc_user()` is the userland path: same byte sinks (UART + framebuffer + VGA + dmesg ring), no timestamp prefix. Kernel printks unchanged. `drivers/video/console/fb_text.ad` ANSI parser now handles `ESC[K` (erase-to-EOL), `ESC[<n>C/D` (cursor forward/back), and `ESC[?25h/l` (cursor visibility) ŌĆö needed by the line editor's redraw. Software underline cursor on the framebuffer. (`3fc58ca`) | Done |
| **atkbd Ctrl-C ŌåÆ SIGINT** | The PS/2 keyboard path now posts `SIGINT` to the foreground process when Ctrl-C produces 0x03. UART path already did this; atkbd was generating 0x03 into the kbd FIFO without raising the signal, so a foreground `yes` ran forever. 0x03 stays in the FIFO so hamsh's line-editor clear-line still works. New `scripts/test_kbd_sigint.sh` drives `qemu-monitor sendkey ctrl-c` and asserts `task: pid N exited (code=130)`. (`adce616`, `7a464b2`) | Done |
| **hamsh init/rc + line editor maturation** | `/etc/rc.boot` is the boot rc, hamsh runs as PID 1 ŌĆö namespace recipe + service launches as plain hamsh statements (`341af32`). Full interactive line editor: cursor editing, history (48-entry ring), Tab completion (command + path), Ctrl-A/E/C, ANSI-escape state machine (`df27310`, `c2a062d`). Plus `[hamsh-alive]` heartbeat (TEMP_DEBUG). | Done |
| **vanilla-ISO install-over-SSH demo** | Four small bundled fixes that make `ssh in ŌåÆ apt install hello` work on a vanilla ISO: `PIPE_MAX` 8 ŌåÆ 32 (so nsrun's distrofs daemons + sshd's bridge coexist), sshd `_bridge_session` closes pipes on every exit path (was leaking 2 fds/session), `/etc/rc.boot` auto-spawns sshd as a detached service, `tcp_smoke_test` gated on `/etc/tcp-smoke-test` so default boots don't ARP-stall in net_smoke pre-`time_init`. End-to-end demo PASSES: SSH publickey auth, apt fetches + SHA-256-verifies + dpkg-unpacks 49 files, 5/5 back-to-back sessions OK. (`0f30263`) | Done |
| **apt streaming over live deb.debian.org** | `_http_stream_gz_index` was treating `sys_read()==0` on TCP as FIN; on `FD_NET_MARK` sockets, zero is ambiguous between real FIN and the 5-second `tcp_recv` timeout-with-no-data. On the real Debian CDN, any TCP-side lull > 5 s killed the stream mid-flight. Fix mirrors sshd `_recv_exact`'s retry-on-timeout idiom (up to 24 idle windows = ~2 min total silence). Live result: `apt-get: streamed gz index (56547292 bytes decompressed)`, `apt-get: fetched index, 68755 packages`, `apt-get: InRelease OpenPGP signature verified`. The full real `stable/main/binary-amd64` archive streamed end-to-end. (`1eeabb1`) | Done |
| **Run-iso launcher + doc refresh** | `scripts/run_iso.sh` interactive launcher (SLIRP networking, framebuffer mode, KVM auto-detect, hostfwd 22ŌåÆ2222). README's "Using hamsh" quickstart with `enter linux { /bin/sh }`, the `debian` alias, errstr try/except, ns/enter/spawn, line-editor keymap, init/rc. `docs/REAL_HARDWARE.md` new ┬¦7 subsection covering bare-metal xHCI auto-skip + decision matrix. `docs/HAMSH_SPEC.md` reframed from "design locked" ŌåÆ reference docs for hamsh as shipped. | Done |

**Headline of this wave:** Hamnix boots the default ISO end-to-end on
an Intel NUC with a working keyboard, hamsh prompt, native binaries,
and the linux runtime. SSH from the host into a vanilla ISO works
end-to-end (`apt install hello` over the encrypted channel, 5+ back-
to-back sessions clean). `apt update` ingests the full live
`deb.debian.org stable/main` archive (68,755 packages, GPG-verified).
The marquee scenario ŌĆö "boot a server, SSH in, install something,
serve it" ŌĆö is one chunked-apt-cache fix away from `apt install
<large-pkg>` working end-to-end against the real Debian archive; agent
`a747ba7f` is in flight on that piece.

## Wave ŌĆö 2026-05-24..26: preemption + L-shim hardening + real-Debian-apt migration + FS-discovery

This wave delivers the structural fix that unblocked everything since,
then sweeps across the .ko shim catalog hardening it, then makes the
biggest architectural correction since the kernel-relocation:
hand-rolled `user/apt.ad` + `user/dpkg.ad` + `user/dpkg_deb.ad` are
DELETED in favor of running real Debian apt/dpkg inside the linux
namespace, and the rootfs moves out of the kernel ELF cpio onto a
separate ext4 partition (live-USB-style layout) so distro content
isn't capped by the FAT12 ~250 MB ceiling. The wave closes with a
clean FS-discovery surface (named file servers via sentinel, by-id
alias for persistent references, `/proc/fs/by-name` inspection).

| Item | Description | Status |
|------|-------------|--------|
| **Preemption (`kernel_cond_resched`)** | NUC boot was wedging after sshd "listening on port 22" ŌĆö no heartbeat, no SSH, frozen. Bisect agent identified `0f30263` (`spawn detached bootns { sshd }`) as the trigger and `drivers/net/tcp.ad`'s `tcp_accept` busy-poll as the structural root: SYSCALL entry clears `EFLAGS.IF`, the LAPIC timer can't fire mid-syscall, `jiffies` is frozen, the `while get_jiffies() < deadline` loop degenerates to `while True`, CPU pinned. Strategic fix: `kernel_cond_resched()` (sti + hlt + cli + schedule-if-ready), wired into all 5 `tcp.ad` busy-poll sites + `dns.ad` + `e1000e_traffic.ad` ARP-prime + `icmp.ad` + `udp.ad`. Also rejects the previous "no preemption like NetWare" cooperative model ŌĆö *"We don't want a cooperative scheduler like freaking NetWare"* ŌĆö by wiring `kernel_cond_resched` per spec. `scripts/test_hamsh_heartbeat.sh` catches future regressions. (`b08853e`, `c94eabd`) | Done |
| **xhci re-enabled on bare metal** | The c444044 "auto-skip xHCI on bare metal" was a same-day MISDIAGNOSIS ŌĆö the NUC wedge that motivated it was actually the `tcp_accept` busy-poll fixed two hours later by preemption. Reverted the skip; wired `__SCT__cond_resched` + `__const_udelay` to `kernel_cond_resched()` so any future xHCI handshake busy-spin on real silicon cooperates with preemption. (`2888b7c`) | Done |
| **USB hc_driver / usb_hcd shim + HID class probe** | `xhci_pci_probe ŌåÆ usb_hcd_pci_probe ŌåÆ xhci_init` runs end-to-end via a force-shim override list in the L-shim loader (10 USB entry points routed to Hamnix before stock-`.ko` ksymtab lookup). `usb_hcd` is a 16 KiB kzalloc'd struct, byte-compatible with stock Linux. `hid.ko` + `usbhid.ko` load with `skipped=0`; data path still flows through the pre-existing hand-rolled `xhci_poll ŌåÆ hid_kbd_report ŌåÆ kbd_rx_push` (URB-completion-via-L-shim is a follow-up). On NUC real silicon (2026-05-25): boot to interactive shell + USB keyboard input works. (`f426aee`, `9404fa2`) | Done |
| **sound stack ŌĆö snd_hda load + init** | All 5 snd modules (`snd`, `snd_pcm`, `snd_hda_core`, `snd_hda_codec`, `snd_hda_intel`) now load with `skipped=0` and `init_module=0`. Two infrastructure fixes the sweep surfaced: `kernel/modules_dep.ad` normalizes `-` ŌåÆ `_` in dep tokens to match on-disk underscore filenames (matches Linux `request_module()`); `linux_abi/loader.ad` handles size-0 `.bss` sections (lockdep `__key.N` symbols) and `MAX_LINUX_MODULES` bumped 8 ŌåÆ 16. snd_hda_intel probe reaches 67 cross-module ksymtab calls; codec attach needs real HW. (`63e2d9e`, `92462db`, `0c99126`, `cd075dd`) | Done |
| **NIC harvest validation** | atlantic, alx, sky2, igb, r8169 all LOAD + probe cleanly via the L-shim ŌĆö no new exports needed (prior `b8b5236` / `7591e64` / `25aaca3` already closed the surface). New `docs/loading_vs_working.md` documents the matrix. igb additionally MATCHES PCI ID 8086:10c9 on QEMU's `-device igb` and runs `ndo_open` ŌåÆ 1 netdev opened; proves the shim is truly generic. (`9b0bb81`) | Done |
| **Block stack post-preempt validation** | All 10 ahci + nvme tests audited; native drivers' busy-poll loops use bounded counter shapes (NOT `while get_jiffies() < deadline`), so no preemption-related fixes needed. Test assertions strengthened to match `test_snd_hda_ko.sh`. `test_nvme_io.sh` failure surfaced as the async-work probe gap (separate item). (`2669088`) | Done |
| **nvme async-work probe gap-closing** | Closed 3 gaps in the nvme.ko probe path: `modules.dep` walker now resolves `nvme_core.ko` (was looking for `nvme-core.ko`), `_l_dev_set_name` accepts heap-allocated ctrl_device pointers (was returning -EINVAL), `async_schedule_node` sync-dispatches inline (was a no-op). Result: nvme-core loads, probe returns 0, 77+ cross-module ksymtab dispatches succeed. Full `add_disk` requires `flush_work` + `blk_mq_alloc_tag_set` integration ŌĆö escalated as Option X (minimal NVMe bring-up in the L-shim, like AHCI's bridge approach) vs Option Y (full Linux blk-mq integration). (`a8dfd12`) | Done |
| **Linux namespace `enter linux {ls /}` works end-to-end** | `chan_resolve_prefix` had a trailing-slash bug for root rebinds ŌĆö `bind / /var/lib/distros/default` + open `/` produced `/var/lib/distros/default/` which `_is_initramfs_dir` rejected. Strip the redundant slash. Also added `HAMNIX_HAMSH_RC` env hook for tests that drive hamsh as `/init` without rc.boot. New `scripts/test_linux_namespace.sh` is the regression backstop. (`1765db2`) | Done |
| **Real Debian apt/dpkg migration** | RETIRED `user/apt.ad` (3960 lines), `user/dpkg.ad` (1891 lines), `user/dpkg_deb.ad` (971 lines) + 20 driver test scripts. They were Adder reimplementations of tools that should run as real Debian binaries inside `enter linux { ... }`. New: `build_initramfs.py` stages a curated apt/dpkg closure (~30 files + their `ldd` closure) from `tests/distros/debian-minbase/rootfs/`. Solves the cpio "follow path-component symlinks" issue via usrmerge duplicate planting. `scripts/test_linux_apt_install.sh` asserts real `Debian dpkg 1.22.22 (amd64)` + `apt 3.0.3 (amd64)` actually run. (`0de1c63`, `bcc4a78`, `3ff5bfc`, `40484d4`) | Done |
| **BSS shrink (256 MiB-guest fit)** | distrofs DATA_SLOT_CAP 512 ŌåÆ 64 (32 MiB ŌåÆ 4 MiB pool), dpkg DEB_CAP 16 MiB ŌåÆ 4 MiB + TAR_CAP 1 MiB ŌåÆ 384 KiB, apt PKG_CAP / HTTP_CAP 512 KiB ŌåÆ 256 KiB each. ~42 MiB per-instance BSS savings. Defensive shrink (not heap conversion) because userland has no `SYS_BRK` / `SYS_MMAP_ANON`; documented in [[feedback-compiler-quirks]]. (`32292d3`) | Done |
| **Rootfs partition (live-USB-style layout)** | The kernel ELF embedded a ~60 MiB initramfs cpio of real Debian content; OVMF's FAT12 driver chokes reading it and FAT12 caps the ESP at ~250 MiB. New: separate ext4 partition (`scripts/build_rootfs_img.py` builds via `mkfs.ext4 -d`); `xorriso -append_partition 3 0x83` adds it to the ISO. Kernel `init/main.ad::mount_rootfs_partition()` scans block devices for ext4 magic and registers the partition in the named file-server stack as `#distro` (sentinel-driven; see the next row). ESP back to 32 MiB; UEFI boot < 30 s. (`f136f4b`, `a85ef44`, ...) | Done |
| **FS-discovery: bind src-first + sentinel file-server + named stacks + by-id alias** | The hamsh `bind` wrapper had inverted Plan-9-flavored arg order (`bind /srv '#s'`); flipped to source-first (`bind '#s' /srv`) to match `SYS_BIND(src, dst)` + Linux `mount`. The `#` parser accepts both single-char built-ins (`#c`/`#p`/`#s`/`#/`) and multi-char role names (`#home`/`#distro`/`#apt-cache`). Sentinel file `.hamnix-roots` at each ext4 partition root maps `<word> <relpath>` lines; absent sentinel ŌåÆ anonymous `#partN`. Stack semantics on collision (depth cap 9, reject on overflow). `#by-id/<partuuid>` stable persistent reference. `/proc/fs/by-name/<word>` + `/proc/fs/by-id/<partuuid>` + `/proc/fs/anonymous` inspection. Bind-freeze: `mnttab_bind` now resolves `#<word>` to `#by-id/<partuuid>` at bind time via `_freeze_named_source`, storing the by-id form as the source path so future opens use the stable by-id and subsequent pushes onto `#<word>` don't move existing bindings (`5a40d60`). (`4f3a74b` .. `5a40d60`) | Done |
| **Compiler quirks audit (LANGUAGE.md sequel)** | LANGUAGE.md re-audit found 2 new real bugs: `Ptr[T] + N` codegen is UNSCALED (production callers all use byte arithmetic via cast); `Percpu[Array]` / `Percpu[struct]` aggregates silently lose the `%gs:` per-CPU base (zero production users today; trap is latent). Both flagged with `TODO(adder)` in the doc body, captured in [[feedback-compiler-quirks]]. (`f676865`) | Done |

**Headline of this wave:** Hamnix completes the structural fix
("kernel preemption, no more cooperative wedge class"), drops months
of hand-rolled apt/dpkg reimplementation in favor of running real
Debian binaries inside the Linux namespace, and moves the distro
content onto a separate ext4 partition with a clean Plan-9-shape
file-server discovery (named stacks, by-id aliases, `/proc/fs`
inspection). Real-hardware boot on the NUC confirmed working end-to-
end with USB keyboard via the L-shim USB-HC bridge. Outstanding gaps
are scope items, not architecture: NUC's network silent on real I219,
nvme.ko needs Option X bring-up wiring, hamsh installer needs to
actually install + boot from the installed disk, an in-init service
supervisor (`svc status sshd` style) is desired.



Closes the install-over-SSH loop end-to-end on a real multi-MiB Debian
package. Two structural fixes ŌĆö a streaming xz/dpkg/apt/tmpfs/distrofs
pipeline and a 16├Ś msize bump across 9P/pipe/sockpair ŌĆö bring `libc6`
(13 MiB unpacked) under the QEMU test budget. A small kernel-side
spawn-path fix lands the SSH TIER-3 round-trip: `ssh user@vm 'uname'`
returns the output over the encrypted channel.

| Item | Description | Status |
|------|-------------|--------|
| **LANGUAGE.md audit** | Audited every section of `LANGUAGE.md` against `compiler/codegen_x86.py` + grep across all 387 `.ad` files. ~14 documented-but-fictional features deleted (lambdas, `try`/`except`, list comprehensions, f-strings, `match`/`case`, class methods, `sizeof` builtin, default args, `with`-statements, decorators, dict/list/tuple/optional types, unions, `volatile T`, qualified imports). 4 missing real features added (Heap Allocation with `kmalloc`/`kfree`/`kzalloc`, Per-CPU Storage, `container_of`, design-principles preamble). Classes section rewritten ŌĆö production uses `ptr[0].field`, not `.field` (the old doc claim would not have compiled). New host-side fixture `scripts/test_compiler_unsupported_rejected.sh` compiles one snippet per deleted feature and asserts codegen rejects each ŌĆö permanent backstop against silent re-introduction. (`b385a4b`) | Done |
| **Streaming xz/dpkg/apt/tmpfs/distrofs pipeline** | `lib/xz/xz.ad` now ships two entry points sharing one LZMA core: the existing buffered `xz_decompress(src, len, dst, dst_cap)` plus a new `xz_decompress_streaming(src, len, drain: Fn[int32, Ptr[uint8], uint64])` that hands decompressed bytes to a first-class callback in 64 KiB chunks. Per-block CRC32 streams incrementally. xz dict bumped to 8 MiB to match Debian's `lzma2 preset=6`. `dpkg` / `dpkg_deb` / `apt` switched from "slurp whole `data.tar.xz`, then unpack from one giant buffer" to drain-callback streaming. `fs/tmpfs.ad` uses a page-chain inode storage scheme instead of the previous 512 KiB-per-file cap. `distrofs` RAM cache sizing re-derived from observed inode count. Plus a small xz inner-loop speedup: ring-modulo replaced with bitmask-AND (`fface2c` / cherry-pick `10f0748`). (`ebce787`, `10f0748`) | Done |
| **9P / pipe / sockpair msize 8 KiB ŌåÆ 128 KiB** | `apt install libc6` was correctness-correct after the streaming refactor but timed out at QEMU's 600 s budget. Root cause: every `sys_write` from dpkg's tar drain into `/usr/...` traverses the kernel 9P client to the `distrofs` daemon, and `P9_MSIZE_DEFAULT=8192` split each 64 KiB tar chunk into ~8 Twrite round-trips. `SOCKPAIR_CAP=1024` and `PIPE_CAP=1024` forced wake-cycle churn on each round-trip. Bumped `P9_MSIZE_DEFAULT` / `P9C_MSIZE` / `SRV_BUF_CAP` / `PIPE_CAP` / `SOCKPAIR_CAP` to 131072 across `lib/9p/9p.ad`, `sys/src/9/port/9p_client.ad`, `user/distrofs.ad`, `user/p9srv_demo.ad`, `init/p9_smoke.ad`, `fs/pipe.ad`, `fs/socketpair.ad` ŌĆö both sides of every 9P/pipe link must agree, and the userland scratch buffers must hold one msize, so the bumps are interdependent. Also replaced `distrofs::_serve_twrite`'s byte-by-byte payload copy with an 8-byte-word `_bcopy` helper. (`4191250`) | Done |
| **libc6 installs end-to-end** | `scripts/test_apt_install_libc6.sh` now PASSES on a clean build. The test boots a QEMU guest, runs `apt update` against a local Debian-shaped mirror, then `apt install libc6` (the real Debian package ŌĆö 13 MiB unpacked, 49 files, including `/usr/lib/x86_64-linux-gnu/libc.so.6`). The full pipeline (HTTP fetch ŌåÆ SHA-256-verify `.deb` ŌåÆ ar-stream ŌåÆ xz-stream `data.tar.xz` ŌåÆ tar-stream ŌåÆ write into distrofs over 9P) runs under the 600 s budget. The 13 MiB threshold is the first concrete demonstration that the streaming pipeline scales past fixture-sized inputs. (`4191250`) | Done |
| **SSH TIER-3 fd binding** | The native sshd was authenticating + opening channels + bridging hamsh's own prompt + line-edit escapes through to the OpenSSH client cleanly, but when hamsh then `spawn`ed an external command (`uname`) the child wrote to its `/fd/1`, which still resolved to the **inherited PID-1 console binding** rather than sshd's `pipe_out[1]`. Two-layer fix: (1) kernel-side, the legacy integer-fd `SYS_SPAWN` path now gives the child a private Pgrp (deep-copied from parent ŌĆö mtab is preserved, so nsrun/apt/dpkg still see parent mounts) and walks `fd 0/1/2` on the child `TaskStruct`, calling `devfd_bind_pipe_r/w` or `devfd_bind_cons` to mirror those backings into `/fd/0,1,2` in the child's Pgrp. New `SYS_FDSLOT_KIND` (287) syscall lets userland query whether an `/fd/N` slot is bound. (2) userland-side, hamsh's `_setup_fd_namespace` checks `sys_fdslot_kind` before binding cons, so it doesn't clobber a kernel-seeded pipe binding. `scripts/test_sshd.sh` PASSES through TIER 3: full SSH round-trip with `uname` output coming back over the encrypted channel. (`525d333`, `a64b2b1`) | Done |
| **Orchestrator lesson: grep before brief** | The sshd-TIER-3 work surfaced a meta-learning: `user/sshd.ad` (2078 lines + `lib/ssh/sshcrypto.ad` + `lib/ssh/sshsign.ad`) already shipped at `03a3a18` and was wired into `/etc/rc.boot` at `0f30263`. Half an agent slot was spent re-discovering this. Saved to orchestrator memory as `feedback_grep_before_brief.md` ŌĆö before any "build X" brief, grep `user/<x>.ad lib/<x>/ drivers/*/${x}*.ad` and `git log -- user/<x>*` for existing implementations and shift the brief to "finish/debug" if anything's there. | Done |

**Headline of this wave:** the streaming-pipeline + 16├Ś msize bump
brings a real-world Debian package (`libc6`, 13 MiB) all the way
through `apt install`, and the kernel-side spawn-path fd-binding fix
makes `ssh user@vm 'uname'` return its output over the encrypted
channel. Combined with the prior install-over-SSH demo, the full
marquee scenario ŌĆö **boot ISO ŌåÆ SSH in ŌåÆ `apt install <multi-MiB
Debian package>` ŌåÆ run a remote command ŌåÆ see its output** ŌĆö works
end-to-end on a vanilla ISO with no env-var overrides. `LANGUAGE.md`
is now a doc agents can trust 100% and a permanent backstop fixture
prevents silent re-introduction of deleted features. The end-game
demo target ("`apt install nginx` and `curl` from the host") is now a
matter of letting the existing pipeline ride a daemon launch ŌĆö no
new architecture needed.

## Wave ŌĆö 2026-05-26..27: hpm v1 + Debian-installer + Plan-9 security model + Adder repo split

This wave is the structural step from "a working ISO" to "a real
distro": the Adder compiler is extracted to its own
[`HamnixOS/adder`](https://github.com/HamnixOS/adder) repo and
consumed as a submodule; a Hamnix-native package manager (`hpm`)
ships with five v1 packages live at `https://255.one/`; the installer
becomes a Debian-installer-shape script driven by `hpm` against an
ISO-local mini-repo; a Plan-9-shape security model lands end-to-end
(hostowner uid 1, `/dev/auth` cdev, SHA-512-crypt, per-user namespace
recipes, `newshell` builtin, `svc` uid switching); the in-init
service supervisor gets a `/proc/svc` kernel mirror; and the
`test_installer_full` 4-stage harness PASSES end-to-end (build ISO
ŌåÆ install ŌåÆ reboot from disk ŌåÆ first-boot ext4 grow-to-fit).

| Item | Description | Status |
|------|-------------|--------|
| **Adder repo split + submodule pin** | The Adder compiler + `LANGUAGE.md` moved to a standalone [`HamnixOS/adder`](https://github.com/HamnixOS/adder) repo. Hamnix consumes it as a git submodule at `adder/` pinned to a specific commit; the top-level `compiler/` and `LANGUAGE.md` paths are forwarding symlinks into the submodule, so every build script keeps working unchanged. CI gains `scripts/test_adder_pin.sh` (a drift-check that the submodule HEAD is a real `HamnixOS/adder` commit). The submodule pin reached `8e0e420` over this wave, bundling two compiler features and two bug fixes: (a) **methods** (static methods, auto-`self`, name-mangled `Class__method` free functions, field-flattening method inheritance with first-match-wins, optional `__init__` sugar); (b) `Ptr[T] + N` is now scaled by `sizeof(T)` to match C/Rust pointer arithmetic; (c) `Percpu[Array]` / `Percpu[struct]` aggregates now correctly emit `%gs:` segment access (previously dropped the per-CPU base on aggregate access). Both `TODO(adder)` markers from the prior LANGUAGE.md re-audit are resolved upstream. (`fb5a366` wire submodule, `0a88c6e` remove duplicates, `2cd030f` doc note, `6d7015f` CI drift-check, `e470c81` methods bump, `a57dfab` Ptr+N + Percpu bump) | **Done** |
| **`hpm` v1 ŌĆö Hamnix-native package manager** | Native Adder binary at `user/hpm.ad` (~5,400 lines) implementing the binary-only v1 package format from `docs/packages.md`. Read-only commands first (`refresh`, `list`, `search`, `show` ŌĆö `0b4b75d`), then `install` for trivial cases (`055bcbf`), `remove` + install hooks (`9b1b75a`), a greedy BFS dependency solver with conflict detection (`4e840e5`), `update` + `pin`/`unpin` (`65e6685`), and verbose progress messages (`a23e3fb`). Repo schemes supported: `https://`/`http://` (over `/net`) and `file://` (local; used by the installer). All `hpm` write commands gate on uid==1 (`8721866`) ŌĆö a regular user gets a clean `hpm: package installation requires hostowner. Try \`newshell hostowner\`.` error. Five packages live at the canonical repo `https://255.one/`: `hamnix-hello` (smoke test), `hamnix-base` (OS userland), `hamnix-bootloader` (kernel ELF + EFI stub), `hamnix-installer-tools` (binaries `install.hamsh` needs), `linux-debian-12` (curated Debian rootfs tree). Verified by `scripts/test_hpm.sh` (refresh/install/list/remove + conflict negative test, `61a128e7`). | **Done** |
| **Installer rewrite ŌĆö `hpm`-driven, Debian-installer shape** | `etc/install.hamsh` is now a 7-step `hpm`-driven installer (per user direction 2026-05-26: *"the install process then becomes a bunch of package manager commands; instead of a DD"*). The ISO carries a mini-repo at `/iso-packages/` baked into the cpio (`2aef0fd`, `257f981`, `02c4fa9` slim mode); the installer (a) probes target/source disks, (b) lays down GPT + partitions, (c) `mkfs_fat` ESP + `mkfs_ext4` rootfs (partition cdevs not whole-disk per `414243a`), (d) `hpm refresh` against `file:///iso-packages/`, (e) `hpm install hamnix-base hamnix-bootloader hamnix-installer-tools linux-debian-12` with `--target-prefix` + `#esp` target support (`a1a69cc`), (f) `dd_blk` source partitions onto target partitions (the source was built from the same v1 packages, so the target is byte-equivalent), (g) prompts for hostowner credentials (`HAMNIX_HOSTOWNER_USER`/`PASSWORD`) and plants `/etc/passwd` + `/etc/shadow` on the installed system. **All four stages of `scripts/test_installer_full.sh` PASS**: build ISO ŌåÆ install ŌåÆ reboot from disk ŌåÆ first-boot ext4 grow-to-fit-1G + second-boot idempotency. (`c2e3dd2`, `762365e`, `b05aeb4`, `b47dbe0`, `9d47686`, `298f678`) | **Done** |
| **Plan-9-shape security model ŌĆö v1** | The `docs/security.md` spec landed (`17e8264`) and was implemented end-to-end across 12 phases. **Hostowner uid 1** (`live` on the live ISO, user-chosen on the installed system; `/etc/passwd` + `/etc/shadow` with `$6$<salt>$<sha-512-crypt>`); `lib/passwd/passwd.ad` + `lib/passwd/shadow.ad` parsers (`75214c1`); a glibc-compatible `lib/crypt/sha512_crypt.ad` (`0bb5f3c`); **`uid`/`gid` on `TaskStruct`** + new syscalls `SYS_GETUID=288`, `SYS_GETGID=289`, `SYS_SETUID=290` (hostowner-only) (`cf041e5`); the kernel-side **`#auth` cdev** at `/dev/auth` (`sys/src/9/port/devauth.ad`, `f5e9982`) where userland writes `user <name>\npass <plaintext>\n` and reads back `ok`/`denied` ŌĆö the only userland path that consults `/etc/shadow`, rate-limited against brute force; **VFS open/create/exec permission check** against owner/group/other rwx (`931bf0d`); **ext4 owner/group/mode** stamped at inode-create + `ext4_mkfs` lays down the root as hostowner (`b42c243`); hamsh gains `read [-s] VAR` and `newshell <user> [-c <cmd>]` builtins (`deb8bb1`), `newshell` reads `/etc/passwd` + prompts password + writes to `/dev/auth` + `rfork`s + sets the child's uid + execs hamsh which loads `/etc/users/<name>.ns` (`43d7499`); `hpm install/remove/update/pin/unpin` gate on uid==1 (`8721866`); the in-init service supervisor (`init/svc`-shape) switches uid before exec (sshd runs as system uid 2; `363263d`); `/etc/users/default.ns` is the restricted regular-user recipe (`ac0bf0d`); the live ISO bakes `live:hamnix`; the installer prompts for hostowner credentials (`ac0bf0d`). Smoke-tested by `scripts/test_security.sh` (Phases 1/4/5/6/7/8/9 ŌĆö hostowner vs regular user boundary; `73adead`, expanded header at `ae15032`). | **Done** |
| **/proc/svc service-supervisor kernel mirror** | The in-init service supervisor (hamsh's `svc` builtin and `/etc/svc/<name>.hamsh` parser, plus the supervisor reap+backoff loop and on-failure backoff ŌĆö `7c967b9`, `ccfed18`, `45a286b`, `419174f`, `4176357` from the prior wave) holds the live svc registry in PID 1's address space. To make `cat /proc/svc/<name>` work for shell-grep / scripting inspection, a parallel kernel-side mirror gets published via a new `SYS_SVC_PUBLISH=291` syscall (hostowner-only, same rationale as `SYS_SETUID`). `fs/procfs.ad` renders `/proc/svc` (bare = all services, one line per registered svc) and `/proc/svc/<name>` (per-service detail matching `svc status`). The supervisor calls `sys_svc_publish` on every state mutation, keeping the mirror in sync. (`124dda6`, `035d781`) | **Done** |
| **ext4 first-boot grow-to-fit + resize wiring** | The installed rootfs ext4 partition is created small (sized to the installed content) and grown to the disk size on first boot. `fs/ext4.ad` gains `ext4_resize_grow` extending block-count + group-descriptor table + bitmaps (`f12b33a`), plus a geometry probe + safety preflight (`1c19819`) and a fix for `bg_flags` / `bg_itable_unused` on new resize groups (`780bdd4`); `init/main.ad`'s `_first_boot_grow_check` wires it up and plants the `.hamnix-grown` sentinel (`3e45ec4`, `fb3a7d7`). The stage D-1G resize loop turned out to be a stale-build artifact (resolved by `298f678` which preserves logs on failure). Verified by `scripts/test_installer_full.sh` Stage D-1G: ext4 grows to fit the installed disk + second boot is idempotent (`c4ab0e5`). | **Done** |
| **UEFI boot speed measured + `ISO_BOOT_TIMEOUT` 30ŌåÆ20** | A measured UEFI boot timing pass (`docs/BOOT.md` ┬¦"UEFI boot timing (measured)"): 5 s from QEMU launch to the deepest asserted marker (cpio registered) under OVMF + 32 MB FAT12 ESP + `HAMNIX_CPIO_LEAN=1`. The 22 MB SFSP read of the kernel ELF runs at ~16 MB/s (already optimal ŌĆö a single `EFI_FILE_PROTOCOL.Read` over the whole buffer, no chunking). With ~6├Ś host-load headroom against the slowest asserted marker, `scripts/test_iso_qemu.sh`'s default `ISO_BOOT_TIMEOUT` drops 30ŌåÆ20 s. (`1b3bdc2`) | **Done** |
| **`test_named_stack` flake fix** | The named-file-server-stack test was flaking because it used blind sleeps. Ported to the `qemu_drive` harness with readiness-marker pacing ŌĆö deterministic PASS. (`935f20c`) | **Done** |

**Headline of this wave:** Hamnix grows the structural pieces of a
real distro: a native package manager (`hpm`) with five v1 packages
live on the canonical repo, an installer rewritten as `hpm install`
calls (the full 4-stage `test_installer_full` regression PASSES
end-to-end including ext4 grow-to-fit), a Plan-9-shape security model
top-to-bottom (hostowner uid 1, `/dev/auth` cdev, SHA-512-crypt,
namespace-as-authority, `newshell`, no setuid bits), and `/proc/svc`
mirror for shell-grep inspection of the in-init service supervisor.
The Adder compiler + `LANGUAGE.md` moved to its own
[`HamnixOS/adder`](https://github.com/HamnixOS/adder) repo consumed
here as a submodule; the pin bump bundles language methods +
`Ptr[T]+N` scaling + `Percpu` aggregate fixes that the LANGUAGE.md
re-audit had flagged. With the installer regression green and a real
package manager in place, the next gate is shipping a stable `0.1`
ISO and onboarding contributors against `https://255.one/`.

## Wave ŌĆö 2026-05-27..28: userland polish push + hpm channels + hamUI Phase 1

A two-day "rough-edges off" sweep took Hamnix from "boots and
installs" to "actually useable as a daily-driver shell." Serial
agent dispatch per user direction (*"don't do it in parallel, too
wide on each issue. Take them one at a time."*), one focused brief
per landed feature.

| Item | What | Status |
|------|------|--------|
| **`hpm` from network ŌĆö DHCP wins, ping ships** | `etc/rc.boot` was unconditionally clobbering the kernel's DHCP-bound IP with a static `10.250.10.99` (a NUC-edge-case fallback baked in too eagerly). Dropped the static; DHCP wins in every other environment (QEMU/SLIRP, GNOME Boxes, home LANs). `hpm refresh` now reaches `https://255.one/` cleanly. New regression `scripts/test_hpm_network.sh`. (`94f57ea`, `ea14914`, `0bdb550`) | **Done** |
| **ext4 multi-group alloc + 512 MiB files + live mkdir + cp -r** | A latent M16.61 limit (`ext4_alloc_block` only scanned group 0) caused sentinel writes to fail when group 0 filled. Extended both alloc and free to scan all groups (`3448ce0`). The long-standing M16.64 single-block write cap then fell ŌĆö `ext4_write_open_file` streams across blocks, growing the inline extent leaf; files up to **512 MiB** (was 4 KiB). Bonus: O_TRUNC and unlink no longer leak blocks past block 0 (`a9b74dd`, `a7bd236`, `11d4b06`, `d2ed204`, `4f2def0`, `2abaf4b`). `vfs_mkdir` for `/ext/*` wires to `ext4_mkdir_live` (was EROFS); `ext4_open_create_or_trunc` rewritten subdir-aware so `cp -r` to `/ext/` lands fully (`b358cb1`, `674c248`, `69d08df`, `f42c9d3`, `85678dd`). | **Done** |
| **Installer: dd_blk ŌåÆ manifest-driven per-file install** | New `ext4_install_file_to_slot` primitive writes one file into an UN-mounted ext4 partition with save/restore of singleton mount globals (`a2b84c5`, `3df8013`, `b046cb6`, `1a1b97b`). Then `etc/install.hamsh` step 6 swapped from `dd_blk vdap4 ŌåÆ vdbp2` to `install_rootfs_from_manifest`, with the manifest generated by `scripts/gen_install_manifest.py`. New kernel helpers: `ext4_mkdir_at_slot`, `_ext4_walk_path_mkdir_p`, `ext4_blob_save_at_path`, `_ext4_dir_create_child` (`e643062`, `aecb48e`, `56335a2`, `5e61106`). ESP/FAT12 side still uses `dd_blk` (separate followup). | **Done** |
| **Component-package split ŌĆö 17 packages + `hamnix-base` metapackage** | The monolithic `hamnix-base` (30-file blob) split into 15 logical components: `hamnix-kernel`, `hamnix-init`, `hamnix-hamsh`, `hamnix-coreutils`, `hamnix-net`, `hamnix-svc-sshd`, `hpm`, `hamnix-fs-ext4`, `hamnix-fs-fat`, `hamnix-drivers-{net-e1000e, block-ahci, block-nvme, usb-xhci, snd-hda}`, `hamnix-installer-tools` + `hamnix-bootloader` + `linux-debian-12` unchanged. `hamnix-base` is now a metapackage; hpm's existing BFS dep solver pulls every leaf via `depends:`. `TMPFS_MAX_FILES` bumped 256ŌåÆ1024 to fit the install closure. (`70ed290`) | **Done** |
| **Subdirectory channels at `255.one/` (Debian-shape)** | Per user 2026-05-27: *"non-free repo... I was thinking more of just a subdirectory; top level directories that each equate to a repository you can subscribe to."* Restructured `HamnixOS/packages` from flat to `/main/` + `/non-free/` + `/non-free-firmware/`. `hpm channels` / `enable` / `disable` subcommands; `/etc/hpm/channels` + `/var/lib/hpm/channels` (default: `main` only). Per-pkg `channel` field routes installs. Live: 17 packages at `https://255.one/main/index.json`; placeholders at the other two channels. (`fcc1641`, `cff568a`, `bf6179a`, `7f25aac`, `b06c8e7`; `HamnixOS/packages` commits `38f2c33` + `0a640ea`; build_packages.py `ensure_ascii=False` at `db00cb3`). | **Done** |
| **`man` + `help` discovery system** | ~20 markdown pages at `/usr/share/man/<topic>.<N>.md` (sections 1/4/5/8). `user/man.ad` opens + cats; `user/help.ad` walks the directory + extracts H1 summaries (`help` alone) or delegates to `man` (`help <topic>`). In-shell `help` builtin deleted in favour of `/bin/help` so it accepts args. (`8503b1e`, `1cf57b8`, `cb44aa5`, `0f3fbe8`, `5f1a7ff`, `eb73777`, `0d53243`, `0ca6a9f`) | **Done** |
| **Real-time `date` + `/proc/realtime`** | RTC driver (`drivers/rtc/cmos.ad`) already existed; added `/proc/realtime` procfs endpoint (`<ISO-8601> <epoch>\n<uptime.cs> <jiffies>\n`); rewrote `user/date.ad` from "uptime stand-in" to real UTC. Wall-clock = `rtc_boot_epoch + tsc_monotonic_ns()/1e9`. (`e5eb459`, `ebd8c24`, `10cc8f1`, `a54c03c`) | **Done** |
| **Persistent svc logs at `/var/log/svc/<name>.log`** | Each managed service's stdout+stderr captured for the lifetime of the boot, append semantics across `svc restart`. Plan-9-shape: new `DEVFD_FILE_APPEND` cdev kind + `OPENCHAN_APPEND` open mode + `tmpfs_open_for_append`. Child stdio binds via `/fd/1`+`/fd/2` namespace bind (NOT Linux dup2). (`2264e92`, `4f8b794`) | **Done** |
| **hamsh builtin redirects** | `echo "foo" > /tmp/x` silently dropped the redirect because builtins bypassed `_wire_redirects`. Fixed via in-process `sys_dup2` save/restore (no fork): 10 builtins now honour `>`/`>>`/`<`/`2>`/`2>&1`. Bonus latent fix: external `>>` was using `OPENCHAN_TRUNC` (silently truncating); now correctly routes through `OPENCHAN_APPEND` + `DEVFD_FILE_APPEND`. (`18d0f51`, `bdb23ec`, `c8d1b72`, `34457b6`, `abd9107`) | **Done** |
| **hamUI Phase 1 ŌĆö AI-debuggable file tree per window** | Renamed `docs/rio.md` ŌåÆ `docs/hamUI.md` (Plan 9 name collision; design overlay H-┬¦A through H-┬¦F captured before implementation). Phase 1 ships `/dev/wsys/1/{text,output,cmd,ns,pid,uid,kind,geometry}` + `/dev/wsys` listing. Strategy: **kernel-side tee on `devcons_write`/`_read` into wsys rings + cmd queue** ŌĆö ZERO hamsh refactor required. End-to-end cmd-injection round-trip works: an external `echo "ls /etc" > /dev/wsys/1/cmd` arrives at hamsh's readline indistinguishable from a keystroke. 12/12 assertions PASS. Multi-window-ready. (`cda060e`, `abae723`, `025c7b1`, `32bb867`, `8f833cd`, `425486a`, `df962fe`) | **Done** |

**Headline of this wave:** Hamnix crossed from "shippable distro
skeleton" to "useable Unix/TempleOS competitor + Plan-9-useable"
per user goal. ext4 went from 4 KiB-cap files to 512 MiB; the
installer dropped its dd_blk crutch; packages split into 17
components published via Debian-shape subdirectory channels at
`https://255.one/main/`; `date` prints real time; man/help solves
discoverability; `>` works on builtins; persistent svc logs hit
disk. And the strategic deliverable ŌĆö **hamUI Phase 1, the AI-
collaboration unlock** ŌĆö landed: an AI agent can `cat
/dev/wsys/1/text` to see what's on the user's screen and
`echo cmd > /dev/wsys/1/cmd` to drive it. Next-up (in flight at
the close of the wave): hamUI Phase 2 multi-window + `/dev/urandom`
+ NTP client.

## Wave ŌĆö 2026-05-28: power management + parallel-track resumption

Trajectory reaffirmed with user (*"Ultimately I wanna do it all. We
can parallelize however possible."*): pursue every track ŌĆö native
hamUI, the Linux X11 bridge, the CLI "survival primitives", and the
U-series Linux userspace ABI ŌĆö choosing each agent by surface
disjointness rather than a fixed priority order. Agents run on
`claude-opus-4-8`.

| Item | What | Status |
|------|------|--------|
| **Real shutdown / reboot / halt / poweroff** | The three power binaries were print-only stubs. Now both a Plan-9-native `/dev/reboot` cdev (`DEV_REBOOT=26`) and the Linux `reboot(2)`=169 syscall funnel into one shared `arch/x86/kernel/power.ad::power_action()` core. It flushes filesystems first (`vfs_fsync_all` + per-block-device `blk_flush`), then: **poweroff** = ACPI-S5 ports `0x604`/`0xB004`/`0x4004` then `cli;hlt`; **reboot** = i8042 `0xFE` pulse with triple-fault fallback; **halt** = `cli;hlt`. `reboot(2)` validates the real Linux magics and is hostowner-gated. `user/{poweroff,halt,reboot}.ad` rewritten to write the verb to `/dev/reboot`. New regression `scripts/test_poweroff.sh` asserts the VM actually exits (not hangs) ŌĆö both poweroff and reboot legs PASS. (`7ec38e8`, `2600da0`, `9e7c676`, `d28591b`) | **Done** |
| **Outgoing `curl` + `wget`** | `sshd` listened but nothing dialed out. The full HTTP/HTTPS-over-`/net` client buried in `hpm.ad` was extracted into a shared `user/http9.ad` (URL parse, IPv4-literal + `sys_resolve` DNS, tcp/tls connect via `net9`, GET with Content-Length drain, chunked-detect-and-fail). `hpm` refactored to consume it (no duplication). New `user/curl.ad` (bodyŌåÆstdout, `-i`/`-o`/`-L`) and `user/wget.ad` (bodyŌåÆfile, `-O`). New `scripts/test_curl.sh` fetches HTTPS + HTTP from `255.one` and round-trips a wget save ŌĆö PASS; `test_hpm_network.sh` still PASS after the refactor. ssh *client* deferred (separate protocol stack). (`87f1035`) | **Done** |
| **hamUI Phase 2 ŌĆö multi-window + bg-shell routing** | `/dev/wsys/<N>/` is now wid-parameterised: `namec.ad` parses the window number out of the path and the wid rides the inline chan id's high bits down to the per-wid devwsys rings (no per-window cdev-slot explosion). `SYS_WSYS_ALLOC=293` / `SYS_WSYS_FREE=294` claim/release a wid for a detached child; `/bin/hamUI new\|list\|close` drives it. Background hamsh instances write to their own wid's ring and are gated out of the foreground serial console.
